THE EDITORIAL BOARD 

Born  in  1941  in  Italy,  he  obtained  a degree  in  Medicine  in 
1966 at the University of Milan. He also obtained  the title of 
Specialist  in  Occupational  Medicine  (1969)  and  the  title of 
Specialist  in Chest Diseases (1972), both at the University of 
Milan. 
From  1968  to  1981  he  had  worked  at  the  Occupational 
Health  Institute  ("Clinica  del  Lavoro")  of  the  University of 
Milan, in charge of diagnosis and treatment. He became assi-

s t a nt  professor  on  physiology  at  work  in  1980.  Several 

research activities were carried out during this period on pneumoconiosis (in parti 
cular asbestosis) and on chronic bronchitis and emphysema. He was also responsi 
ble of occupational services at an asbestos mine and at several chemical industries. 
He  joined  the  European  Commission  in  1981  as  principal  administrator  at  the 
Industrial  Medicine  and  Hygiene  Unit (now Occupational  Health  apd Hygiene) of 
the Public Health and Safety  Directorate. 
He  is  responsible  for  the  scientific  management  of  the  ECSC  Medical  Research 
Programmes  and  is  involved  in  some  proposals  for  Council  Directives  (limit 
values, prohibitions, carcinogens, biological agents, chemicals). Other activities are 
related to the evaluation of risks linked to the exposure to dangerous agents. 
Since  1990  he  has  been  secretary  of  the  Toxicology  Section  of  the  "Scientific 
Advisory  Committee  to  examine  the  Toxicity  and  Ecotoxicity  of  Chemical 
Compounds". 
More than 60 scientific papers have been published either in specialized  magazines 
or in Congress Acta. Since  1978 he has been  member of  the editorial  board of the 
"Medicina del Lavoro" magazine. 

Walter  Karcrl 

Born  in  1931  in  Germany,  he  obtained  a  degree  (TU 
Karlsruhe) and a doctorate (TU Berlin) in chemistry. 
At  present,  Dr.  Karcher  is  responsible  of  the  European 
Chemicals Bureau, Environment Institute, at the Joint Research 
Centre of the European Commission in Ispra (Italy). 
Previous  tasks  in  the  frame  of  the  EC  Activities  include  a 
secondment to the OECD High Temperature (Helium cooled) 
!  Reactor  Project  at  UKEA  Winfrith  (UK,  1962-65)  and 
various activities at JRC Petten, (NL, 1965-1986, i.e. head of 
Organic  Materials Service  as part  of  the  EC program  on  Reference  Materials and 
Reference Methods). 
Publications  more  than  50  articles  in  Scientific  Literature;  the  series  on  the 
"Spectral Atlas on Polycylcic Aromatic Compounds" (3 volumes); a monograph on 
"Dibenzanthracenes  and  Environmental  Carcinogenesis"  (Cambridge  University 
Press) and two volumes on Structure Activity Relationships (SAR) (co-editor). 
Dr. Karcher is member of the Editorial Board of two scientific journals, "Polycyclic 
Aromatic  Compounds" (PAC) and "SAR  and QSAR  in Environmental  Research", 
and  also  member  of  the  Steering  Committee  for  the  series  of  International 
Workshop on QSAR in Environmental Sciences. 
(Main  organizer  of  the  6th  International  Workshop  on  QSAR,  1994  and  the  15th 
International Symposium on PAC 1995, Belgirate, Italy)

Chemistry  in  1963  and  in  1977  a  doctorate  in  Medical-
Biology at the University of Milan. 
Dr.  Roi  is  employed  as  a  Scientific  Officer  at  the  Joint 
Research  Centre  of  the  European  Commission  in  Ispra  (I). 
For eighteen  years  he has been  responsible  of  the  Industrial

In  1983,  on  behalf  of  the  Health  and  Safety  Directorate  of  the  European 
Commission  (DGV)  in  Luxembourg,  Dr.  Roi  was  a  cofounder  of  the  Editorial 
Board  for  the  publication  of  the  series  entitled  "Biological  Indicators  for  the 
Assessment of Human Exposure to Industrial Chemicals". 
In 1986, in Geneva, together with Prof Luigi Parmeggiani, he created the Scientific 
Committee  of  Data  Banks  in  Occupational  Health,  as  part  of  the  ICOH 
(International Commission of Occupational Health) activities. 
Since 1994 Dr. Roi has been assigned to the University of Pavia by the Ministry of 
Public  Education  of  the  Italian  Government  as  an  Effective  Member  in  the 
Examining Body for post-doctorate qualification  in biological sciences. 

José Maria Si 

Born  in  1932 in  Spain, he obtained  a degree  in Medicine in 
1955 at the University  of  Madrid  and  in  1986 a doctorate in 
Medicine  at  the  Autonomous  University  of  Barcelona.  He 
also obtained  the title of Specialist  in Occupational  Medicine 
at  the  University  of  Madrid  (1970)  and  a  Diploma  of 
Environmental  Engineering  at  the  University  of  Valencia 
(1979). 
Founder  Member  of  the  Spanish  Society  of  Occupational 
Medicine (1955), Dr. Sevilla has been for more than 20 years 
President  of  the  Balearic  Society  of  Occupational  Medicine  and  from  1971  till 
1979  Director  of  the  National  Institute  of  Occupational  Safety  and  Hygiene  in 
Balearic Islands. Since  1979 he has been  Medical  Director  of "Mutua  Balear", an 
Entity of  Insurance of Accidents  of Work  and Professional  Diseases and currently 
is  an  International  Representative  of  AMAT  (the  Spanish  Association  of  the 
Entities of Insurance of Occupational Health). 
Dr. Sevilla has been Chairman of the Scientific  Committee (since  1989) and Board 
Member (since  1993) of the International  Commission  on Occupational  Health. In 
collaboration  with  the  World  Health  Organization  he  publishes  the  International 
Directory of Databases and Data Banks in Occupational Health. 

NOTE TO THE READERS 

In  1973 the  Council  of  Ministers  of  the  European  Communities  stressed  the  need  to 
increase the protection  against dangerous chemicals and to improve the existing tools 
for  documentation  and distribution  of information  in the field  of toxicology, ecotoxi-
cology, health and safety  at the workplace. 

Following  these  recommendations  the  Joint  Research  Centre  (JRC)  initiated  a pro 
gram to evaluate the hazard of chemicals at all level. 

Among several  other  activities  it was decided  to create  a Data  Bank  (Environmental 
Chemicals  Data  and  Information  Network  -  ECDIN  Project*),  in  order  to  have 
access to the information  on the effects  caused  by the impact  of xenobiotics on envi 
ronment, human and animal  life. 

The  Data  Bank  was  realised  with  the  scientific  cooperation  of  several  European 
Toxicological  Centres,  Research  Institutes  and,  perhaps,  a  hundred  of  individual 
experts. 

The  database  of  ECDIN  was  subdivided  into  sub-files  in  view  of  an  homogeneous 
grouping of the scientific  data. One of the main sub-files  of the Data Bank was devo 
ted to the storage of data on BIODEGRADATION  OF CHEMICALS BY AQUATIC 
ORGANISMS. 

The present issue gives an example of the data stored into the Biodegradation  sub-file. 

In this first  version, the text  includes only  experiments  performed  on aquatic organi 
sms. Data on highly  insoluble compounds are not taken into consideration. 

Information  on biodegradation  are focused  to clarify  whether  the substance  is degra 
ded  to non-toxic  molecules  or, vice-versa,  to relatively  persistent  and  toxic interme 
diates. 

The  experimental  data  are  obtained  by  comparing  standard  reference  compounds. 
When possible, the importance of biodegradability  is determined  through  indications 
on the Persistence  Factor. 

In  compatibility  with  the  information  available  in  scientific  literature,  each  experi 
ment  is  covered  with  the  most  important  environmental  variables  which  can  effect 
the  rate  and  extent  of  biodegradation.  The  experiments  are  consequently  reported 
considering the following  parameters: 

•  Biological  System Description  (organism, origin, conditions) 

•  Test Parameters  (parameter  measured,  temperature  PH, salinity, dissolved  oxygen, 

quantity and quality of nutrients, etc.) 

•  Results (initial concentration, time, percentage converted, persistence  factor) 

The conventional  oxidation  parameters, such  as BOD  (Biological  Oxygen  Demand), 
COD  (Chemical  Oxygen  Demand),  TOC  (Total  Oxygen  Demand),  ThOD 
(Theoretical  Oxygen Demand) are mentioned  in most of the experiments. 

The  first  volume  includes  experiments  related  to 91 compounds. These  experiments 
have been  updated  by  means of  consultation  of  42 international  scientific  references 
and data banks. 

The experiments included  in the present issue have been revised by: 

Prof. Franco Cecchi 
Dipartimento di Ingenieria  Chimica 
Università  dell'Aquila 

and 

Dr. Paolo Pavan 
Dipartimento di Scienze Ambientali 
Università di Venezia 

The  first  updating  is  foreseen  in  1996.  It  will  include  more  than  200  chemicals, 
selected among those having a biological significance  in this matter.

European Commission 

EUR  16254 -  Biodegradation of chemicals by aquatic organisms 

G. Aresini,  W. Karcher, R. Roi, J.M. Sevilla Marcos 

Luxembourg: Office for Official Publications of the European Communities 

1995 -  VII, 206 pp. -  16.2 χ 22.9 cm 

Environment and quality of life series 

ISBN 92-827-4244-X 

This volume contains  information on the biodegradation  (i.e. complete  mineralization) 
of  chemicals  by aquatic  organisms. 

The  data  are  referred  to  96  chemicals  listed  in this  first  volume  of  the  biodegra­
dation  series. 
For each  experiment the data comprises  information on: 
•  Species 
•  Exposure concentration  and  time 
•  Test  conditions 
• 
•  Degradation  profile 
•  Bibliographic  reference 

Initial and final concentrations  in various  organs
